The Argument from Necessary Emanation
Author argues that necessary emanation collapses distinction between good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the doctrine of necessary emanation undermines the distinction between good and evil.

Core Idea
If everything is necessary, nothing is truly good or evil.

The author challenges the philosophical view that the universe necessarily emanates from God. He argues that if all existence is a necessary consequence, then the categories of good and evil, essential and accidental, lose their meaning. This passage shows the logical dead end of necessitarian theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key terms and the logical flow.
Pay attention to how the author builds his argument.
2
Identify the opponent's position
The opponent holds that all existence proceeds from God as necessary consequences. Identify where this is stated.
3
Analyze the collapse of distinction
See how the author argues that if everything is necessary, then there is no difference between essential and accidental entailment. This eliminates any real distinction between good and evil.
The author uses the example of harm and benefit to show relativity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل فتنة وآفة صلاح، ولكل حيوان يؤذي خاصية، ومودع في كل جسم من الأجسام منفعة ومضرة، وكل مضرة فبالنسبة إلى شيء آخر منفعة. لكنا نلزمكم أمرًا كليا فإن عندكم الوجود كله بما فيه من الروحاني والجسماني صادر عن الأول على الترتيب المذكور صدور اللوازم عن الشيء، وما كان على سبيل اللوازم فهو بالقصد الثاني أشبه منه بالقصد الأول، فما الفرق بين الشرور الواقعة في الكائنات وكونها مقتضية بالعرض وبين أصل الكون والكائنات وحصولها على سبيل اللزوم؟ فليس إذا في الوجود شيء هو مقتضى بالذات حتى يكون شيء آخر هو مقتضى بالعرض.
Every trial and affliction is beneficial, and every animal that harms has a specific property, and in every body is placed benefit and harm, and every harm is relative to something else a benefit. But we impose upon you a universal matter: for according to you, all existence, including the spiritual and the corporeal, proceeds from the First in the mentioned order as the procession of necessary consequences from a thing, and whatever is by way of necessary consequences is closer to secondary intention than to primary intention. So what difference is there between the evils occurring in beings and their being accidental entailments, and the origin of being and beings and their occurrence by way of necessity? Thus there is nothing in existence that is an essential entailment such that another thing is an accidental entailment.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation of the opponent's position that all existence emanates from God as necessary consequences. The author begins by noting that the opponent already admits that every harm is relative to some benefit. Then he draws a universal conclusion: if all things proceed necessarily as consequences (لوازم) of the First, then there is no distinction between primary and secondary intention. The author asks: what difference can there be between evils that occur accidentally and the existence of the universe itself, if both are necessary? The conclusion is that nothing in existence is essentially intended (مقتضى بالذات) as opposed to accidentally intended (مقتضى بالعرض); all are equally necessary. This collapses the opponent's attempt to justify evil as accidental.

Key Terms
لوازم
قصد
مقتضى بالذات
مقتضى بالعرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is denying relative good and evil.
Correction: He is showing that necessity eliminates the distinction between essential and accidental, not denying relativity.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what follows from the opponent's view that all existence emanates necessarily?
A) Some things are essentially intended and others accidentally.
B) There is no distinction between essential and accidental entailment.
C) Evils are only apparent, not real.
D) The world is created by chance.

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of necessary emanation strips existence of any real moral or teleological distinction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage argues that if everything is a necessary consequence of God, then nothing is truly good or evil in an absolute sense. Think of a painful trial you have faced. Is it possible that your labeling of it as 'bad' is only relative, and that from God's perspective it is as 'necessary' as any blessing? What does this realization demand from you in terms of your trust in God's wisdom?
?
The author collapses the distinction between essential and accidental intentions. Do you ever find yourself making excuses for your own sins by saying they were 'unintentional' or 'accidental'? In light of this lesson, does that excuse hold any weight if all actions are equally within God's creation? How does this change how you take responsibility before God?
?
If there is no essential intention behind anything, then even your most sincere acts of worship become merely necessary consequences. Does this possibility trouble you? How does the Islamic doctrine of free will and God's creative act preserve the meaning of your intention (niyya) in a way that this opponent's system cannot? Let this question drive you to deepen your understanding of the relationship between God's creation and human accountability.

Refutation of Philosophers on Evil and Three Disputed States
Refutation of philosophers on evil and listing three disputed states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic refutation of the philosophers' claim that evil is not widespread, and the three points of dispute regarding the existence of a pure source of evil, the prevalence of good, and the basis of created things.

Core Idea
Evil is real in human acts but not in divine acts; the philosophers' denial contradicts experience, revelation, and reason.

Imam al-Shahrastani refutes the philosophers who argue that evil is not widespread. Drawing on Quranic verses, empirical observation, and rational principles, he shows that evil predominates in human choices. He then identifies three key points of disagreement that must be settled before the philosophers' position can stand.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Begin by reading the three Quranic verses cited at the start. They establish that most people are ungrateful and disobedient, contradicting the philosophers' claim that evil is rare.
The verses are referenced in the Arabic text.
2
Understand the rule of fitra vs acquisition
The author presents a general rule: when divine decree and innate disposition dominate, good prevails; when human choice and acquisition dominate, evil prevails. This explains why evil is common in human actions.
3
Consider scriptural and rational proofs for evil entities
The passage affirms the existence of devils and Iblis, supported by prophetic miracles. Even ancient philosophers and dualists acknowledged a universal principle of evil.
The author references his own work 'al-Milal wa al-Nihal' for dualist views.
4
Examine the three disputed states
The author lists three key points where philosophers disagree: (1) denial of a pure essence of evil, (2) claim that good is more prevalent in humans, and (3) affirmation of existents without a foundation. These must be refuted for their position to hold.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that unless these three principles are established, the philosophers' argument fails. The passage reaffirms that evil exists in human acts but not in divine acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَعْقِلُونَ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٦٦]، ﴿ وَمَا وَجَدْنَا لأَكْثَرِهِم مِّن عَهْدِ وَإِن وَجَدْنَا أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَفَسِقِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۰۲]، ﴿ وَقَلِيلٌ مِّنْ عِبَادِيَ الشَّكُورُ ﴾ [سبأ: ۱۳]، فكيف يستمر لكم معاشر الفلاسفة أن الشر في العالم بمطلقه لا يوجد وبأكثره لا يتحقق، وقد صادفتم الوجود على خلاف ما قررتم، فاعتبروا النفوس الإنسانية والغالب على أحوالها من العلم والجهل وعلى أخلاقها من الحسن والقبيح، وعلى أقوالها من الصدق والكذب، وعلى أفعالها من الشر والخير تعلمون أن الشر في العالم الجسماني أغلب وأكثر خصوصا في النفوس الإنسانية. وبالجملة فحيث ما وجدنا الفطرة والتقدير الإلهي غالبا على الاختيار والاكتساب البشري، كان الغالب هو الخير والصلاح، وحيث ما وجدنا الاختيار والاكتساب غالبين كان الغالب هو الشر والفساد، فعاد الأمر إلى أن لا شر في الأفعال الإلهية، فإن وجد فيها شر فبالإضافة إلى شيء دون شيء، وإنما يدخل الشر في الأفعال الإنسانية الاختيارية وهي أيضا من حيث إنها تستند إلى إرادة الباري سبحانه خير، ومن حيث إنها تستند إلى اكتساب العبد تكتسب اسم الشر، غير أن الشرائع قد وردت بإثبات الشياطين وإثبات رأسهم إبليس اللعين، وليس يمكن إنكار ذلك بعد ثبوت الصدق في أقوالهم وأخبارهم بالبينات الواضحة والمعجزات الباهرة، وقد اعترف بوجودها قدماء الحكماء قالوا: ما من شيء جزئي في العالم إلا ويتحقق له في عالم آخر أمر كلي، فبالحرارة الجزئية استدل على نار كلية، وبالعقل الجزئي يستدل على عقل كلي، وكذلك سائر الأمور فبالشر الجزئي في العالم يستدل على شر كلي. وكذلك أثبت المجوس وأصحاب الاثنين للعالم أصلين هما منبع الخير والشر والنفع والضرر وهما النور والظلمة كما سبق ذكر مذاهبهم، وقد استوفيناها في كتابنا الموسوم بالملل والنحل وبالجملة الفلاسفة منازعون في ثلاثة أحوال: أولها نفي محض موجود هو أصل الشر بالذات لا بالعرض، والثاني كون الخير في النوع الإنساني أكثر وأغلب، والثالث إثبات موجودات لا مستند لها على طريق الإيجاد بالذات بالقصد الأول، وما لم تثبت هذه الأصول لم يتم لهم ما ذكروه، والله أعلم وأحكم.
They do not understand [Quran 2:166], and We did not find for most of them any covenant, and indeed We found most of them to be defiantly disobedient [Quran 7:102], and few of My servants are grateful [Quran 34:13]. How can it continue for you, O group of philosophers, that evil in the world does not exist at all and is not realized in its majority, while you have encountered existence contrary to what you have determined? So consider human souls and what prevails over their states of knowledge and ignorance, and over their morals of good and evil, and over their sayings of truth and falsehood, and over their actions of evil and good; you will know that evil in the corporeal world is more prevalent and more abundant, especially in human souls. In summary, wherever we find innate disposition (fitra) and divine decree predominating over human choice and acquisition, what predominates is good and righteousness; and wherever we find choice and acquisition predominating, what predominates is evil and corruption. So the matter returns to that there is no evil in divine actions; if evil is found in them, it is relative to something rather than something else. Evil only enters into voluntary human actions, and they too, inasmuch as they are attributed to the will of the Creator, are good; and inasmuch as they are attributed to the acquisition of the servant, they acquire the name evil. However, the revealed laws have come affirming the devils and affirming their chief Iblis the accursed, and it is not possible to deny that after the establishment of truthfulness in their sayings and reports through clear proofs and dazzling miracles. And the ancient sages acknowledged their existence; they said: There is no particular thing in the world except that it has in another world a universal order; so from particular heat they inferred a universal fire, and from particular intellect they inferred a universal intellect, and likewise for all other things; so from particular evil in the world they infer a universal evil. Similarly, the Magians and the dualists affirmed for the world two principles that are the source of good and evil and benefit and harm, namely light and darkness, as their doctrines were mentioned before; and we have exhaustively treated them in our book titled al-Milal wa al-Nihal. In summary, the philosophers are disputed in three states: first, a pure negation of a being that is the principle of evil by essence not by accident; second, that good in the human species is more and more prevalent; third, the affirmation of existents that have no basis for their existence by way of essential creation with the first intention. And unless these principles are established, what they have mentioned is not completed for them. And God knows best and is most wise.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' claim that evil is not widespread or does not exist in the world. The author begins by citing Quranic verses that indicate most people are not grateful or faithful, establishing that evil and disobedience are common. He then directly addresses the philosophers, challenging how they can maintain their position when experience shows otherwise. The argument proceeds to examine human souls, morals, speech, and actions, concluding that evil predominates, especially in human souls. The author then provides a general rule: where divine decree and innate disposition (fitra) dominate human choice and acquisition, good prevails; but where human choice and acquisition dominate, evil prevails. He clarifies that divine actions contain no evil; any apparent evil in them is relative. Evil enters only into voluntary human acts, which are good by divine will but acquire the name 'evil' through human acquisition. The author then invokes scriptural proof for the existence of devils and Iblis, stating that they cannot be denied given the clear proofs and miracles of the prophets. He further supports this by noting that ancient sages (philosophers) admitted universal forms corresponding to particular things, including a universal evil. Then he mentions the Magians and dualists who posited two principles of good and evil. Finally, he summarizes the three points of dispute with the philosophers: (1) denial of a pure essence of evil, (2) claim that good is more prevalent in humans, and (3) affirmation of existents without a foundation. The author concludes that without establishing these three principles, the philosophers' position fails.

ملل ونحل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the author denies evil exists in the world.
Correction: The author affirms evil in human acts but denies evil in divine acts; evil is real and widespread in human choices.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does evil predominate?
A) When divine decree and fitra predominate
B) When human choice and acquisition predominate
C) In all cases equally
D) Only in the actions of animals

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' denial of widespread evil is refuted by experience, revelation, and reason; evil exists in human acts but not in divine acts, and three points of dispute remain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent moment when you let your own choice overrule your fitra. What was the outcome, and how did you feel about it? Are you willing to name that evil as your acquisition, not God's will?
?
The passage says evil enters only through voluntary human acts. Look at your own life: where have you blamed God or circumstances for something that was actually your own doing? How would repenting of that specific acquisition change your relationship with Him?
?
The philosophers deny that evil is prevalent, but you and I know the world is full of it. When you see evil in your own heart—like pride, envy, or disobedience—do you truly believe it is your own acquisition? If so, what will you do today to take full responsibility before God?

Physical Causality of Sound
From acoustic events to the ear's reception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two physical causes of sound—strike and rupture—and how sound waves reach the ear.

Core Idea
Sound arises from violent air movement caused by striking or rupturing bodies.

This passage begins with the physical origin of sound. The author describes two mechanisms—strike and rupture—that generate vibrations in the air. Understanding this causal chain is essential for grasping how sensory perception leads to higher knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the detailed description of the two causes.
2
Identify the two types of sound generation
Find where the author explains sound from strike (قرع) and from rupture (قلع). Note the different processes.
Strike compresses air, rupture releases air.
3
Trace the wave propagation to the ear
Follow the description of how the wave reaches the ear canal (صماخ) and causes ringing. Note the mention of the nerve and drum analogy.
4
Reflect on the role of the ear's structure
Consider why the author includes such detail about the ear's anatomy. This shows that physical hearing is a prerequisite for cognition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأول ما يرد على السمع حرف وصوت يحصل في الهوى بسبب تموج يقع بحركة شديدة تحدث من قرع بعنف أو قلع بحدة، فإن كان من قرع اصطك الجسمان وانضغط الهوى بشدة وحدث الصوت، وإن كان من قلع انقطع الجسمان وانفلت الهوى بشدة وحدث الصوت، ووصل الموج إلى الهوى الراكد الذي في الصماخ وانفعل به وهو مجاور للعصبة المفروشة في أقصى اصماخ الممدودة مد الجلد على الطبل، فيحصل فيه طنين فتشعر به القوة المودعة في تلك العصبة، فيصل إلى القوة الخيالية فيتصرف الخيال فيه تقديرا ، فيصل إلى القوة النسانية فتتصرف النفس فيه تفكيرًا ، فيصل إلى القوة العقلية فيتصرف العقل فيه تمييزاً وللمعنى صعود من المحسوس المسموع إلى المعقول المعلوم صعودًا من الكثرة إلى الوحدة ونزول من المعقول المعلوم إلى المحسوس المسموع، نزولا من الوحدة إلى الكثرة، والعرفان مبتدئ من تفريق ونفض وترك ورفض ممعن في جمع هو جمع صفات الحق للذات المريدة للصدق، ثم انتهى إلى الوحدة ثم وقوف، وهذا من حيث الصعود والعرفان مبتدئ من توحيد وتفكير
And the first that reaches the hearing is a letter and a sound that occurs in the air due to an undulation that takes place through a strong movement resulting from a forceful strike or a sharp rupture. If it is from a strike, the two bodies clash and the air is compressed severely and sound occurs. If it is from a rupture, the two bodies separate and the air is released severely and sound occurs. And the wave reaches the stagnant air in the ear canal (ṣimākh) and is affected by it, which is adjacent to the nerve spread in the deepest part of the ear canal, extended like the stretching of skin over a drum. Then a ringing occurs in it, and the power deposited in that nerve senses it. It reaches the imaginative power, and the imagination acts upon it by way of estimation. Then it reaches the human (nafsānī) power, and the soul acts upon it by way of thought. Then it reaches the rational power, and the intellect acts upon it by way of discrimination. And for meaning (al-maʿnā) there is an ascent from the sensed heard to the intelligible known, an ascent from multiplicity to unity, and a descent from the intelligible known to the sensed heard, a descent from unity to multiplicity. And gnosis (al-ʿirfān) begins from separation, shaking off, leaving, and rejecting, deeply engaged in a gathering which is the gathering of the attributes of Truth for the essence desiring truth. Then it ends at unity, then a pause. This is from the perspective of ascent. And gnosis begins from tawḥīd and thought.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage explains the causal process of hearing from physical acoustic events to cognitive processing. Sound originates from a strong movement in the air due to either a strike (قرع) or a rupture (قلع). The wave propagates to the ear canal (صماخ), where it impacts the stagnant air and causes a ringing sensation in the auditory nerve. This sensation is then processed by the imaginative faculty (القوة الخيالية) through estimation (تقدير), then by the psychological faculty (القوة النفسانية) through thought (تفكير), and finally by the rational faculty (القوة العقلية) through discrimination (تمييز). The author then draws a broader epistemological and metaphysical conclusion: meaning (المعنى) has an ascent from the multiplicity of sensed particulars to the unity of intelligible universals, and a descent from unity back to multiplicity through utterance. Gnosis (العرفان) begins with a process of separation and rejection, then moves to a gathering of the divine attributes, culminating in unity. The passage emphasizes the integration of sensory perception, cognition, and spiritual knowledge, showing how the physical process of hearing is linked to intellectual understanding and ultimately to divine gnosis.

Key Terms
صوت
هوى
صماخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sound only requires air and does not involve the ear's structure.
Correction: The author details how the ear canal and nerve are essential for hearing.

Checkpoint
What are the two physical causes of sound mentioned in the passage?
A) Strike and rupture
B) Compression and expansion
C) Vibration and resonance
D) Air and water

Key Takeaway
Sound is physically produced by either a strike or a rupture causing air movement, which then travels to the ear.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the adhān or Qur'ān, do you ever pause to consider that this sound reaches you through a precisely ordered chain of physical causes—strikes, ruptures, air waves, and nerves—all created by Allah? How would your listening change if you consciously remembered this chain every time you heard His words? This week, try to bring that awareness to one recitation you hear and note the difference in your heart.
?
Your ear contains a nerve spread 'like skin over a drum,' designed to sense the ringing of sound. What does this intricate design tell you about the One who fashioned it? Are you using your hearing primarily for what pleases Him, or have you allowed it to be filled with heedless noise? Make a specific commitment today to guard your ears from one type of harmful sound you habitually expose them to.

Cognitive Processing of Sound: Imagination, Thought, and Reason
From sensory input to rational discrimination via three faculties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three cognitive faculties—imagination, psychology, and reason—that process sound after it is sensed.

Core Idea
Hearing involves not just the ear but a chain of mental faculties: imagination, thought, and reason.

After the sound is sensed by the ear, it is passed through three internal powers: the imaginative faculty (قوة خيالية), the psychological faculty (قوة نفسانية), and the rational faculty (قوة عقلية). Each performs a different operation: estimation, thought, and discrimination. This passage shows that human cognition is a layered process.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three powers mentioned in sequence.
2
Identify the three faculties
List the imaginative, psychological, and rational powers. Note the Arabic terms.
The psychological power is also called 'qūwa nafsāniyya'.
3
Understand their functions
The imagination performs estimation (تقدير), the soul performs thought (تفكير), and the intellect performs discrimination (تمييز). Reflect on the progression.
4
Consider the overall point
The author shows that hearing is not merely physical but involves higher cognitive processes, leading to rational understanding.

Source Text

?

?

Ascent and Descent of Meaning and Gnosis
The metaphysical ascent and descent of meaning and the path of gnosis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ascent of meaning from sensed multiplicity to intellectual unity and the descent back, and how gnosis begins with separation and culminates in tawḥīd.

Core Idea
Gnosis ascends from multiplicity to unity and descends back, beginning with rejection and ending with oneness.

The passage concludes with a profound epistemological and metaphysical reflection. Meaning (المعنى) has an ascent from the sensed heard to the intelligible known, moving from multiplicity to unity, and a descent from unity to multiplicity. Gnosis (العرفان) begins with separation and rejection, then gathers the attributes of Truth, ending in unity. This shows the integration of sensory knowledge with spiritual realization.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the terms 'صعود' (ascent), 'نزول' (descent), and 'عرفان' (gnosis).
2
Understand the ascent of meaning
Meaning ascends from the multiplicity of sensed sounds to the unity of intelligible knowledge.
3
Understand the descent of meaning
Meaning descends from unity back to multiplicity, perhaps through expression or teaching.
4
Grasp the nature of gnosis
Gnosis begins with separation and rejection, then gathers the attributes of Truth, and culminates in unity (tawḥīd).
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
The entire process from physical hearing to rational discrimination is linked to the spiritual journey of gnosis.

Source Text

Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage explains the causal process of hearing from physical acoustic events to cognitive processing. Sound originates from a strong movement in the air due to either a strike (قرع) or a rupture (قلع). The wave propagates to the ear canal (صماخ), where it impacts the stagnant air and causes a ringing sensation in the auditory nerve. This sensation is then processed by the imaginative faculty (القوة الخيالية) through estimation (تقدير), then by the psychological faculty (القوة النفسانية) through thought (تفكير), and finally by the rational faculty (القوة العقلية) through discrimination (تمييز). The author then draws a broader epistemological and metaphysical conclusion: meaning (المعنى) has an ascent from the multiplicity of sensed particulars to the unity of intelligible universals, and a descent from unity back to multiplicity through utterance. Gnosis (العرفان) begins with a process of separation and rejection, then moves to a gathering of the divine attributes, culminating in unity. The passage emphasizes the integration of sensory perception, cognition, and spiritual knowledge, showing how the physical process of hearing is linked to intellectual understanding and ultimately to divine gnosis.

Key Terms
صعود
نزول
عرفان
صفات الحق
توحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does gnosis (العرفان) begin with?
A) Unity and gathering
B) Separation and rejection
C) Thought and descent
D) Sound and sensation

Key Takeaway
Meaning ascends from sensed multiplicity to unified knowledge, and gnosis begins with rejection and ends in divine unity.

You read that gnosis ends in 'unity, then a pause'. Have you ever experienced a pause in your spiritual journey—a moment of stillness after striving? If not, what keeps you restless? If you have, how did that pause change you?

The passage says gnosis begins with tawḥīd and thought. Do you treat tawḥīd as a mere statement you repeat, or as the active foundation that reshapes your everyday thinking? What one thought today can you consciously anchor in tawḥīd to begin that ascent?

The Second Objection: Can Composition Alone Explain All Properties?
Presents the second objection that all actions' properties are due to composition, except perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the materialist objection that all actions' properties stem from composition, and why the author concedes everything except perception.

Core Idea
All properties except perception can be explained by composition.

The author presents a powerful objection: if composition yields amazing properties in stones, plants, and numbers, why need a soul? He concedes everything except one unique property: perception. This sets up the defense of the soul's immateriality.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author starts by conceding the opponent's points, then asks a rhetorical question.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the examples
The author lists many properties from stones, plants, animals, and even abstract numbers (magic squares) to show that composition alone produces amazing effects.
These examples challenge the need for a soul.
3
Find the single exception
The passage ends with 'except for one thing: its perception' – this is the crucial point. All other properties may be due to composition, but perception is unique.
Perception (idrāk) is what distinguishes the soul.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why perception cannot be explained by composition. This sets up the author's response in the next part.
The author implies a dualism: material composition vs. immaterial perception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الاعتراض الثاني على خواص الأفعال التي ذكروها هو أنا نسلم كل ما قرروه ولكن نقول بم تنكرون على من رد ذلك كله إلى كمالية التركيب في المزاج وخاصية التأليف الواقع بين الأمشاج إذ غرف من خواص الجوهر غرائب وعجائب أحوال لا يرتقي إليها الوهم ولا يرتمي نحوها العقل والفهم من تسكين وتحريك وحل وعقد وتنمية وإذبال وجذب وإرسال وتسخير وتدبير وحب وبغض وتصحيح وإمراض وإحياء وإماتة ما يقضي منه العجب ألا ترى من خواص الأحجار وخواص النبات والأشجار وهدايات الحيوانات إلى مصالحها ما لا يقصر في الدرجة عن خواص النفس الإنسانية ألا تعتبر من تأليفات الأعداد المجردة عن المادة مثل أعداد الوفق وغيرها كيف يؤثر في الأجسام حتى قيل إن النفس الإنسانية عدد تأليفي كل ذلك من كمالية التأليف والتركيب وكما أن الأجرام البسيطة بما هيأتها ذوات خواص كذلك المركبات بتأليفها ذوات خواص فبتأليف أكمل ترتقي المعادن والنبات على العناصر وبتأليف أفضل يرتقي الحيوان والإنسان على المعادن والنبات فما دليلكم أن هاهنا سوى التأليف الأفضل والتركيب الأكمل نفسا روحانية فإن جميع الخواص التي عددتموها يمكن حملها على كمالية التركيب فقط سوى شيء واحد وهو إدراكه
As for the second objection concerning the properties of actions that they mentioned: it is that we concede everything they established, but we say: On what basis do you reject one who attributes all of that to the perfection of composition in the mixture and the specific property of the composition occurring between the mixtures? For we know from the properties of the substance strange and wondrous states that imagination does not ascend to, nor does intellect or understanding approach them: from calming and moving, dissolving and binding, growth and decay, attraction and repulsion, subjugation and management, love and hate, health and illness, life and death—things that amaze. Do you not see from the properties of stones, properties of plants and trees, and the guidance of animals to their benefits, what does not fall short in degree from the properties of the human soul? Do you not consider from the compositions of numbers abstracted from matter, such as magic square numbers and others: how they affect bodies, so much so that it was said: The human soul is a compositional number. All of that is from the perfection of composition and combination. And just as simple bodies by their constitution possess properties, likewise compounds by their composition possess properties. By a more perfect composition, minerals and plants rise above the elements, and by a superior composition, animals and humans rise above minerals and plants. So what is your proof that besides the superior composition and the more perfect combination there is a spiritual soul? For all the properties you enumerated can be attributed to the perfection of composition alone, except for one thing: its perception.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection concerning the properties of actions (khawāṣṣ al-afʿāl). The author first concedes the opponent's previous points, then asks: Why not attribute everything to the perfection of composition (kamāliyyat al-tarkīb) and the specific property of composition? He gives examples of amazing properties in substances, stones, plants, animals, and even abstract numbers like magic squares, all of which arise from composition. He argues that just as simple bodies have properties, compounds have more elevated properties due to composition. So, what proof is there for a spiritual soul apart from composition? He concludes that all properties can be attributed to composition alone, except for one thing: perception (idrāk). This suggests that perception may be the unique property of the soul.

If perception is the one thing not reducible to composition, then your awareness of this very question is a sign of something immaterial. Al-Jubba'i's Argument and the Ash'ari Objection on Conditions
Presents Al-Jubba'i's argument and the Ash'ari objection on conditions for perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Jubba'i's argument for direct perception without an additional attribute and the Ash'ari objection that physical conditions are necessary for perception.

Core Idea
Perception requires more than just being alive.

Al-Jubba'i argued that a living being free from defects perceives everything equally, proving no separate idrak is needed. The Ash'ari school objected that perception in this world depends on physical structure and transparent media, so the same conditions must hold for God's perception. This passage presents both positions and highlights a key difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument come through.
The passage has two clear parts: the argument and the objection.
2
Identify Al-Jubba'i's proof
Look for how Al-Jubba'i argues that a sound essence perceives all accidents equally, and why he rejects a separate perception attribute.
His key point is that if there were a separate idrak, it could perceive one thing but not another.
3
Identify the Ash'ari objection
Notice how the objectors grant perception in the witnessed world but deny that life alone suffices. They list physical structure and medium as additional conditions.
They use the analogy of the three senses to force a similar requirement for sight and hearing.
4
Understand the rhetorical strategy
The objection forces the opponent to either prove that only life is needed or accept that life is a merely habitual condition like physical structure.
This is a classic Ash'ari tactic to limit the scope of the argument.
5
Reflect on the difficulty
The passage ends by noting this is a difficult issue. Consider why the problem of perception conditions is challenging for theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الجبائي : إن الحي إذا سلمت نفسه عن آفة سمي سميعاً بصيراً والدليل عليه : أن الذات إذا سلمت أدركت كل معروض عليها من المتماثلات والمختلفات وإدراكها السواد كإدراكها البياض ولو كان مدركا بإدراك لجاز أن يدرك بعض الأشياء دون بعض مما يقابل المدرك فكان يجوز أن يدرك بياضا ولا يدرك سوادا وهما متقابلان للحاسة في حالة أو حالتين متعاقبتين كما أن العالم منا جاز أن يعلم شيئا دون شيء قالوا وإن سلمنا ثبوت الإدراك في الشاهد فلم نسلم أن المصحح مجرد كون الحيوان حيا فقط وهاهنا شرط آخر وهو حصول البنية وشرط للشرط وهو توسط الهوى المضيء بين المبصر والمبصر والهوى الصافي بين السمع والمسموع كما في الشم واللمس والذوق اتصال الأجرام ومماستها بالاتفاق وإذا استدعت الثلاث من الحواس شرطا حتى يتحقق الإدراك ولأجل ذلك امتنع إثباته غائبا كذلك الحاستان الباقيتان استدعتا شرائط أخر سوى كونه حيا حتى يتحقق الإدراك فأنتم مدفوعون إلى إقامة الدليل على حصر الشرائط في كونه حيا فقط وإلا فارفعوا كون الحياة شرطا كما رفعتم كون البنية وتوسط الهوى شرطا واجعلوا وجود الحياة شرطا من حيث العادة لا من حيث الضرورة كما جعلتم البنية شرطا من حيث العادة وهذا الموضع من مشكلات مسائل الإدراكات
Al-Jubba'i said: Indeed the living being, if its soul is free from defect, is called hearing and seeing. The proof for that is: when the essence is sound, it perceives every accident presented to it, both similar and different; its perception of black is like its perception of white. If it were perceiving by a perception, it would be permissible that it perceive some things but not others of what confronts the perceiver, so it would be permissible that it perceive whiteness and not perceive blackness, even though both confront the sense in one state or two successive states, just as the knowledgeable among us may know one thing but not another. They said: Even if we grant the existence of perception in the witnessed world, we do not grant that the enabler is merely the fact that the animal is alive; rather there is another condition here, namely the existence of physical structure, and a condition for that condition, namely the intervening luminous air between the seer and the seen, and the clear air between hearing and the heard, just as in smell, touch, and taste there is contact and contiguity of bodies by consensus. And since the three senses require a condition for perception to occur, for that reason its existence in the unseen is impossible; likewise the remaining two senses require other conditions besides being alive for perception to occur. So you are driven to provide proof that the conditions are restricted to being alive only; otherwise, remove life as a condition just as you removed physical structure and the intervening air as conditions, and make the existence of life a condition by habit not by necessity, just as you made physical structure a condition by habit. And this point is among the difficult issues of the problems of perceptions.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage contains two parts: first, Al-Jubba'i's argument for direct perception; second, the Ash'ari objection. Al-Jubba'i argues that a living being free from defect is called hearing and seeing without any additional attribute, because if the essence is sound, it perceives all accidents equally – black and white are perceived the same. If perception were by a separate idrak, then it could perceive one but not the other even though both are present, which is absurd. The objection, introduced by 'They said', is that even if we grant perception in the witnessed world, we do not grant that the only enabling factor is being alive. Rather, physical structure and medium (air, contact) are necessary. Just as the three senses (smell, touch, taste) require contact, so do sight and hearing require transparent medium. So the opponent must prove that only life is needed; otherwise, they should treat life as a merely habitual condition, not a necessary one. The passage ends with a note that this is a difficult issue.

الهوى الصافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Jubba'i denies any conditions for perception.
Correction: Al-Jubba'i does not deny conditions; he argues that the only condition is life, while the objection maintains additional physical conditions are required.

Checkpoint

A) Perception requires an additional attribute called idrak.
B) A sound essence perceives all accidents equally without needing a separate perception.

D) The senses require physical structure.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jubba'i's argument for direct perception is countered by the Ash'ari claim that perception requires physical structure and medium, making it impossible to prove that God perceives without such conditions.

?
Al-Jubba'i assumed life is sufficient for perception, but the Ash'ari objection shows we cannot transfer our limited experience to Allah. Where in your life have you measured Allah by your own standards, assuming He must act as you do? Repent today for such limitation of your Lord and ask Him to teach you His transcendence.
?
The passage calls this a difficult issue. When you face theological questions that seem beyond your understanding, does your heart become impatient or do you submit to Allah's wisdom? Commit to seeking knowledge with humility, accepting that some matters are beyond human grasp.

Refutation of the Ray Theory of Vision
The author refutes the ray theory of vision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical and physical arguments that refute the ray emission theory of vision.

Core Idea
Vision does not occur by rays shooting from the eye.

This passage presents a sophisticated critique of the ancient theory that vision works by beams emitted from the eye. The author dismantles this view through multiple arguments, showing its physical impossibility, logical contradictions, and empirical failures. By examining these refutations, you will see how classical Islamic scholars engaged with natural philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the ray theory
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the theory being refuted: that rays are luminous bodies emitted from the eye.
Notice how the theory attempts to explain why we see some things and not others.
2
Examine the first argument about size
The author argues that the eye cannot contain bodies as large as half the celestial sphere, whether the rays pre-exist or are created at the moment of observation.
This shows a physical impossibility.
3
Consider the second argument about multiple observers
If rays combine, a weak-sighted person should see better when looking with others, which does not happen in reality.
This is an empirical counterexample.
4
Analyze the third argument about the nature of the ray
The ray cannot be an accident (since accidents don't transfer) nor a substance (since it would either remain connected and get separated, or not remain connected and fail to provide continuous perception).
This is a logical dilemma.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that both the ray theory and the form-emanation theory are false.
Consider how this critique fits into broader discussions about causality and perception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن العجب أنهم كما شرطوا البنية شرطوا في الرؤية اتصال الأشعة وهي أجسام مضيئة تنبعث عن البصر عند فتح الأجفان، وهي أجسام تتشكل وتتحرك وتتعوج وتستقيم، فإذا اتصل الشعاع المنبعث من الناظر بالقاعدة على حد معلوم مع الاستقامة ولم يكن ثم بعد مفرط ولا قرب مفرط أدركه الرائي، فلذلك لا يرى الشيء البعيد على غاية البعد، ولا يرى باطن الأجفان، وإن كانت القاعدة صقيلة ارتدت الأشعة إلى الرائي، فرأى عند ذلك نفسه، وربما يظن أنه ينفصل عن المتلون صورة ويمتد إلى العين فينطبع فيها، وكلا المذهبين باطل. أما القول بالأشعة التي تنبعث من العين فبطلانه بأنا نعلم قطعا أن العين على صغرها لا تتسع لأجسام تنبسط على نصف كرة العالم، فإن تلك الأجسام إن كانت موجودة بالفعل محسوسة بالجفن، فوجب أن يكون قدرها مثل نصف كرة السماء، وهذا محال، وإن حدثت في ساعة الملاحظة فما السبب لحدوثها؟ ومن المعلوم أن القدرة الحادثة لا تصلح لحدوث الأجسام والقول بتولد الأجسام أمحل، ويلزم من ذلك أيضا أن جماعة من ذوي الأبصار أنه اجتمعوا على رؤية شيء وجب أن يقوى إدراك الضعيف البصر الذي معهم، فإن شعاعه إن قل ما في نفسه فقد تكثر بأشعتهم، وإن ضعف عن حالة القوى فقد يقوى باشتراك أشعتهم، فينبغي أن يستعين الضعيف كما يستعين بقوة ضوء السراج. ثم الشعاع إن كان عرضا فيستحيل عليه الانتقال، وإن كان جوهرًا فلا يخلوا إما أن يبقى متصلاً وإما أن لا يبقى فإن بقي فيلزم أن يتفرق ويدرك الشيء متفرقاً، وينبغي أن يكون مثل خط مستقيم يتحرك بتحريك الريح وينقطع بقطع الماء، وإن لم يبق متصلا فلم يدرك العين بما اتصل به، بل بما انفصل عنه، فما اتصل بالمرئي لم يتصل بالعين وما اتصل بالعين لم يتصل بالمرئي فيلزم أن لا يتحقق له إدراك أصلا.
And it is strange that just as they made structure a condition, they made for vision the connection of rays (al-ash‘a‘a) which are luminous bodies emitted from the eye upon opening the eyelids, and they are bodies that form, move, bend, and straighten. When the ray emitted from the observer connects to the base at a known limit with straightness, and there is not excessive distance nor excessive closeness, the observer perceives it. Therefore, a very distant thing is not seen, nor the inside of the eyelids. And if the base is polished, the rays reflect back to the observer, and he then sees himself. And perhaps one thinks that a form separates from the colored object and extends to the eye and is imprinted in it. Both doctrines are false. As for the statement about rays that are emitted from the eye, its refutation is that we know with certainty that the eye, despite its smallness, cannot contain bodies that spread over half the celestial sphere. For if those bodies exist actually, perceived by the eyelid, then their size must be like half the celestial sphere, and this is impossible. And if they occur at the moment of observation, what is the cause of their occurrence? And it is known that a created power is not fit for the occurrence of bodies, and the statement about generation of bodies is most absurd. Also it would follow that if a group of people with sight gather to see something, the perception of the weak-sighted among them must be strengthened, for if his ray is little in itself, it may increase by their rays, and if it is weak relative to its state of strength, it may strengthen by sharing their rays, so the weak person should be aided just as he is aided by the strength of the light of a lamp. Then the ray, if it is an accident, then transmission is impossible for it; and if it is a substance, then it is either that it remains connected or that it does not remain. If it remains, then it follows that it becomes separated and perceives the thing as separated, and it should be like a straight line that moves by the movement of the wind and is cut by the cutting of water. And if it does not remain connected, then the eye does not perceive by what is connected to it, but rather by what is separated from it. So what is connected to the visible object is not connected to the eye, and what is connected to the eye is not connected to the visible object, so it follows that no perception is realized for it at all.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage refutes two theories of vision: the ray emission theory and the form emanation theory. The author first describes the ray theory: luminous bodies (rays) are emitted from the eye upon opening the eyelids. They travel straight to the object, and if conditions of distance and straightness are met, vision occurs. The theory also explains reflections and why very distant objects or closed eyelids are not seen. The author then refutes it with several arguments: (1) The eye cannot contain bodies as large as half the celestial sphere, whether they exist permanently or are created at the moment of observation. Created power cannot produce such bodies. (2) If multiple observers look at the same object, the weak-sighted should have their vision strengthened by the rays of others, similar to using a lamp. (3) The ray, if an accident, cannot transfer; if a substance, it either remains connected (leading to separation and contradictory perception) or does not remain connected (in which case the eye does not perceive through a continuous ray, but through disconnected parts, so perception fails). The author also dismisses the alternative form-emanation theory as false. The passage concludes that both theories are invalid.

Key Terms
شعاع
أشعة
رؤية
بصر
جوهر
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Vision occurs because rays are emitted from the eye and travel to the object.
Correction: The author shows that this is physically impossible and logically contradictory; vision does not involve such emitted rays.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is a consequence of the ray theory if multiple people look at the same object?
A) The object becomes brighter
B) The weak-sighted person should see better due to shared rays
C) The rays cancel each other out
D) The rays cause blindness

Key Takeaway
The ray theory of vision is refuted by multiple logical and physical arguments, showing that vision cannot be explained by emitted rays.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You trust your eyes every day. But this lesson shows that the very mechanism of vision is a matter of divine creation, not physical rays. Are you willing to see every sight you witness as a direct act of Allah, and let that awareness transform your gratitude and humility? What would change in your daily routine if you truly believed that 'seeing' is a miracle created anew each moment?
?
The author dismantles a theory with pure logic, leaving no room for complacency. When was the last time you subjected one of your own beliefs—about religion, life, or yourself—to such rigorous scrutiny? Are you brave enough to question a comfortable assumption today and risk finding it baseless?
?
If the ray theory is false despite its initial plausibility, what other seemingly obvious explanations in your life might be illusions? How will you seek the truth beyond what your senses and common sense tell you, especially in matters of faith and purpose?

Refuting the Ray: Pre-existence and Generation
Shahrastani refutes ray theory via pre-existence and generation absurdities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two key refutations of the ray theory: the physical impossibility of a pre-existing giant ray and the causal problem of its generation.

Core Idea
A pre-existing ray would be impossibly large; a generated ray lacks a cause.

Shahrastani begins his refutation by attacking the physical assumptions of the ray theory. He shows that if the ray already exists in the eye, its size would be absurd. If it comes into being at the moment of sight, there is no plausible cause for its creation. He also points out that if rays from multiple observers combine, a weak-sighted person should benefit, which is not the case. This lesson examines these logical problems.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the entire passage for this lesson. Notice the structure: first argument about pre-existence, then about generation, then about multiple observers.
2
Understand the pre-existence argument
The author claims that if the ray exists in the eye in actuality and is sensed by the eyelid, its size would be half the celestial sphere. Why is that absurd? Because it's physically impossible for an eye to contain such a large beam.
Think about the physical implications.
3
Analyze the generation argument
If the ray arises at the moment of observation, what causes it? The author says temporal power cannot create bodies. Why? Because bodies require a creator with infinite power. The generation of bodies out of nothing is rejected.
This is a theological point about causation.
4
Consider the multiple observers argument
If multiple people look at the same object, their rays should combine to help a weak-sighted person. But we don't observe this. So the ray theory fails empirical test.
Note the analogy with lamp light.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كانت موجودة بالفعل محسوسة بالجفن، فوجب أن يكون قدرها مثل نصف كرة السماء، وهذا محال، وإن حدثت في ساعة الملاحظة فما السبب لحدوثها ؟ ومن المعلوم أن القدرة الحادثة لا تصلح لحدوث الأجسام والقول بتولد الأجسام أمحل، ويلزم من ذلك أيضا أن جماعة من ذوي الأبصار أنه اجتمعوا على رؤية شيء وجب أن يقوى إدراك الضعيف البصر الذي معهم، فإن شعاعه إن قل ما في نفسه فقد تكثر بأشعتهم، وإن ضعف عن حالة القوى فقد يقوى باشتراك أشعتهم، فينبغي أن يستعين الضعيف كما يستعين بقوة ضوء السراج. ثم الشعاع إن كان عرضا فيستحيل عليه الانتقال، وإن كان جوهرًا فلا يخلوا إما أن يبقى متصلاً وإما أن لا يبقى فإن بقي فيلزم أن يتفرق ويدرك الشيء متفرقاً، وينبغي أن يكون مثل خط مستقيم يتحرك بتحريك الريح وينقطع بقطع الماء، وإن لم يبق متصلا فلم يدرك العين بما اتصل به، بل بما انفصل عنه، فما اتصل بالمرئي لم يتصل بالعين وما اتصل بالعين لم يتصل بالمرئي فيلزم أن لا يتحقق له إدراك أصلا.
They were actually existing sensed by the eyelid, so it is necessary that its size be like half the sphere of the sky, and this is impossible. And if they occur at the moment of observation, what is the cause of their occurrence? And it is known that temporal power is not suitable for the occurrence of bodies, and the saying that bodies are generated is more invalid. From that also it follows that a group of sighted people, if they gather to see something, it is necessary that the perception of the weak-sighted among them be strengthened, for his ray, if it is small in itself, may be multiplied by their rays, and if it is weak in state of powers, it may be strengthened by the participation of their rays, so the weak-sighted should seek help just as one seeks help by the strength of lamp light. Then the ray: if it is an accident, then transition is impossible for it; and if it is a substance, it is unavoidable that either it remains continuous or it does not remain. If it remains, then it follows that it splits and perceives the thing as split, and it should be like a straight line that moves with the movement of wind and is cut by the cutting of water. And if it does not remain continuous, then the eye does not perceive by what is connected to it, but rather by what is separated from it. What is connected to the seen is not connected to the eye, and what is connected to the eye is not connected to the seen, so it follows that it does not achieve any perception at all.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage refutes the ray (shu'aa') theory of vision, which holds that sight occurs via a beam emitted from the eye. The argument proceeds in two parts. First, the author considers the physical properties of the supposed ray. If it pre-exists in the eye, its size would be enormous (half the celestial sphere), which is absurd. If it arises at the moment of sight, no cause can explain its sudden generation, since finite power cannot create bodies. The author also argues that if multiple observers combine their rays, a weak-sighted person should be helped, which is not observed. Second, the author analyzes the nature of the ray: if it is an accident, it cannot travel from eye to object; if it is a substance, it must either remain continuous or not. If continuous, it would split up to perceive a thing as fragmented, which is false. If not continuous, the part reaching the object never connects to the eye, so no perception occurs. Thus the theory is impossible.

Key Terms
شعاع (ray)
قدرة حادثة (temporal power)
تولد (generation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ray theory of vision is scientifically plausible.
Correction: Shahrastani shows it leads to absurdities: a pre-existing ray would be impossibly large, and a generated ray has no cause.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem if the ray pre-exists in the eye?
A) It would not be able to leave the eye.
B) Its size would be half the celestial sphere, which is impossible.
C) It would be too small to see.
D) It would be an accident.

Key Takeaway
The ray theory is refuted because a pre-existing ray would be impossibly large and a generated ray lacks a cause, and multiple rays do not combine to aid vision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The ray theory seemed plausible to many, yet it was refuted with clear logic. In what areas of your life have you accepted something without examining its foundations? Will you commit to questioning your assumptions more rigorously starting today?
?
The weak-sighted person cannot rely on others' rays to see. Do you depend on others' faith or knowledge to compensate for your own spiritual weakness? What one step will you take to strengthen your own connection to truth?
?
If a generated ray lacks a cause, then all events must have a cause. Do you live with the awareness that your every action has a cause and consequence? How might you align your daily choices with the reality that nothing happens without reason?

The Ray as Accident or Substance: Logical Contradictions
Shahrastani refutes ray theory by analyzing its metaphysical nature as accident or substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how categorizing the ray as either accident or substance leads to logical contradictions that refute the emission theory of vision.

Core Idea
Whether accident or substance, the ray cannot account for coherent perception.

Having attacked the ray's origin, Shahrastani now examines its nature. He argues that the ray cannot be an accident because accidents do not travel. If it is a substance, it must either remain continuous or not. Both possibilities lead to absurdities: continuous rays would split perception, and discontinuous rays would disconnect eye from object. This lesson unpacks these decisive arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the second part of the original passage. Focus on the dilemma: accident vs. substance, and the two subcases for substance.
2
Understand why the ray cannot be an accident
Accidents cannot move from one substrate to another. If the ray is an accident in the eye, it cannot travel to the object. So the theory fails.
This is a basic metaphysical principle in kalam.
3
Examine the continuous substance case
If the ray is a substance that remains continuous, it would have to split to cover the object, resulting in fragmented perception. Also, it would behave like a physical object vulnerable to wind and water, which is not how vision works.
The author uses reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the discontinuous substance case
If the ray does not remain continuous, then the part that touches the object is not connected to the eye. Therefore, the eye does not receive any information from that part, so perception cannot occur.
This is a logical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كانت موجودة بالفعل محسوسة بالجفن، فوجب أن يكون قدرها مثل نصف كرة السماء، وهذا محال، وإن حدثت في ساعة الملاحظة فما السبب لحدوثها ؟ ومن المعلوم أن القدرة الحادثة لا تصلح لحدوث الأجسام والقول بتولد الأجسام أمحل، ويلزم من ذلك أيضا أن جماعة من ذوي الأبصار أنه اجتمعوا على رؤية شيء وجب أن يقوى إدراك الضعيف البصر الذي معهم، فإن شعاعه إن قل ما في نفسه فقد تكثر بأشعتهم، وإن ضعف عن حالة القوى فقد يقوى باشتراك أشعتهم، فينبغي أن يستعين الضعيف كما يستعين بقوة ضوء السراج. ثم الشعاع إن كان عرضا فيستحيل عليه الانتقال، وإن كان جوهرًا فلا يخلوا إما أن يبقى متصلاً وإما أن لا يبقى فإن بقي فيلزم أن يتفرق ويدرك الشيء متفرقاً، وينبغي أن يكون مثل خط مستقيم يتحرك بتحريك الريح وينقطع بقطع الماء، وإن لم يبق متصلا فلم يدرك العين بما اتصل به، بل بما انفصل عنه، فما اتصل بالمرئي لم يتصل بالعين وما اتصل بالعين لم يتصل بالمرئي فيلزم أن لا يتحقق له إدراك أصلا.

And it is known that temporal power is not suitable for the occurrence of bodies, and the saying that bodies are generated is more invalid. From that also it follows that a group of sighted people, if they gather to see something, it is necessary that the perception of the weak-sighted among them be strengthened, for his ray, if it is small in itself, may be multiplied by their rays, and if it is weak in state of powers, it may be strengthened by the participation of their rays, so the weak-sighted should seek help just as one seeks help by the strength of lamp light. Commentary
This passage refutes the ray (shu'aa') theory of vision, which holds that sight occurs via a beam emitted from the eye. The argument proceeds in two parts. Refutation of the Image Transfer Theory
Shahrastani refutes the theory that perception occurs by transfer of an image from the object to the eye.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the theory that perception involves the transfer of an image from the object to the eye is rationally impossible, and how the kalam alternative of perception as a 'meaning' (ma'na) avoids these absurdities.

Core Idea
Perception is not a physical transfer; it is a meaning that arises in the sense organ.

Shahrastani tackles a common early theory of vision: that an image literally travels from the seen object into the eye. Using a crisp dilemma, he shows this leads to impossible consequences. This passage illustrates the kalam method of refuting claims by reductio ad absurdum and establishes a foundational principle: perception is a non-material meaning (ma'na) in the sense organ.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the argument.
The passage is a refutation that uses a two-pronged argument.
2
Examine the first objection
Notice the reductio: if an image transferred from fire, the eye would burn. This is absurd because we see fire without being burned.
3
Examine the second objection
The image must be either an accident or a substance. Neither can transfer without absurd consequences. Understand the kalam concepts of accident and substance.
Accidents cannot migrate loci; substances would cause diminishment.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that perception is a meaning (ma'na) in the sense organ, not a transferred entity. This is a key kalam doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول بانتقال صورة من المرئي إلى البصر باطل أيضا، فإن الصورة لو انتقلت لاحترقت العين برؤية النار، وهي إن كانت عرضا فهي لا تنتقل، وإن كانت جوهرًا فلينقص المرئي بانفصال شيء منه، ولا ينفصل شيء منه إلا بسبب، هاهنا فهو باطل، فتحقق أن الإدراك معنى في حاسة المدرك.
And the saying that an image transfers from the seen to the sight is also false. For if the image transferred, the eye would be burned by seeing fire. And if it is an accident, it does not transfer; and if it is a substance, then the seen would decrease by the separation of something from it, and nothing separates from it except by a cause; here it is false. So it is established that perception is a meaning (ma'na) in the sense organ of the perceiver.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage refutes the theory that vision occurs by an image (surah) traveling from the object to the eye. The author gives two objections. First, if the image transferred, then seeing fire would literally burn the eye, which does not happen. Second, the image must be either an accident or a substance. If an accident, it cannot transfer from one locus to another. If a substance, then the seen object would diminish each time it is seen, which is false. Since no valid mechanism exists, the theory is false. The conclusion is that perception is a meaning (ma'na) that inheres in the sense organ, not a transferred entity.

Key Terms
صورة (image)
انتقال (transfer)
عرض (accident)
جوهر (substance)
معنى (meaning)
حاسة (sense organ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Perception occurs by a physical image traveling from the object to the eye.
Correction: This would cause absurdities like burning from fire and diminishment of objects; perception is a meaning in the sense organ.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would happen if an image of fire transferred to the eye?
A) The eye would be burned.
B) The image would become an accident.
C) The object would increase.
D) The sense organ would become luminous.

Key Takeaway
Perception does not involve physical transfer; it is a meaning that inheres in the sense organ.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at something forbidden, do you tell yourself it's just an image entering your eyes? Knowing that perception is a meaning you actively register, how does this change your responsibility in guarding your gaze? What step will you take today to protect the meanings entering your heart through your sight?
?
You have read that the image does not physically transfer, yet you still feel its effect. In what specific area of your life have you allowed a harmful image to linger 'within you' as if it were a permanent substance? What is one concrete action you can take to remove that meaning and replace it with something pure?

Philosophers' Theory of Sense Perception and the Mechanism of Sight
Philosophers explain sense perception via forms and illustrate with sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' account of how sense perception occurs, especially sight, through forms emanating from the Bestower of forms.

Core Idea
Perception is not direct contact but forms imprinted in the senses.

This passage presents the philosophers' detailed causal theory of sense perception. They argue that forms emanate from the Bestower of forms when the sense and the sensible object face each other. Using sight as a concrete example, they explain how images form in the eye and are then perceived in the common sense. Let's examine their account step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once. Focus on the flow of the argument from the general principle to the specific example of sight.
The passage is dense; do not worry about understanding every detail yet.
2
Identify the key components
Identify the main elements: the Bestower of forms, the external senses, the icy moisture of the eye, the seeing power, and the common sense. Notice how they relate to one another.
The term 'wahib al-suwar' is central to the theory.
3
Analyze the mechanism of sight
Work through the example of sight. Understand the mirror analogy, the rejection of emission theories, and the path of the image from the eye to the brain.
The distinction between the image in the eye and perception in the common sense is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت الفلاسفة: يرتسم في الحواس الظاهرة بصور صورة تفيض عليها من واهب الصور عند استعدادات تحصل فيها بمقابلة الحاس والمحسوس، ثم قد تكون تلك الصورة نفس الإدراك، وقد يكون الإدراك شيء آخر دون تلك الصورة؛ كمقابلة المرئي من الألوان والأشكال في الرطوبة الجليدية من العين التي تشبه البرد والجمد فإنها مثل مرآة، فإذا قابلها متلون انطبع مثل صورته فيها كما ينطبع مثل صورة الإنسان في المرآة بتوسط جسم شفاف بينهما، لا بأن ينفصل من المتلون شيء ويمتد إلى العين ولا بأن يتصل شعاع فيمتد إلى المتلون، فإذا حصلت الصورة في الجليدية أفضت إلى القوة الباصرة المودعة في ملتقى الأنبوبتين في مقدم الدماغ، وهما عصبتان مجوفتان على شكل صليب فتدركه النفس بهما، فتكون الصورة في الجليدية من العين والإدراك في الحس المشترك.
And the philosophers said: an image is imprinted in the external senses, a form that flows upon them from the Bestower of forms when preparations occur in them by the facing of the sense and the sensible. Then that image may be perception itself, or perception may be something other than that image – like the facing of the visible thing of colors and shapes in the icy moisture of the eye, which resembles cold and ice, for it is like a mirror. So when a colored object faces it, a likeness of its form is imprinted in it just as the likeness of a human form is imprinted in a mirror by means of a transparent body between them – not by anything separating from the colored object and extending to the eye, nor by a ray connecting and extending to the colored object. So when the image occurs in the icy moisture, it passes to the seeing power deposited at the junction of the two tubes in the front of the brain – they are two hollow nerves in the shape of a cross – so the soul perceives through them. Thus the image is in the icy moisture of the eye, and perception is in the common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak).
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' theory of sense perception, specifically that forms emanate from the 'Bestower of forms' (Wahib al-Suwar) when the sense and sensible object face each other. The author then explains sight as a concrete example. The eye contains an icy moisture that acts like a mirror; the form of the colored object imprints onto it without any physical emission or ray. This image then passes to the seeing power located in the brain, where the soul perceives through two hollow nerves arranged like a cross. The key distinction is made: the image resides in the eye's moisture, but perception occurs in the common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak), which is internal.

Key Terms
الفلاسفة (philosophers)
واهب الصور (Bestower of forms)
الحس المشترك (common sense)
الجليدية (icy moisture)
القوة الباصرة (seeing power)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that philosophers denied perception as a mental act, believing it occurs entirely in the sense organ.
Correction: The passage clarifies that although the image forms in the eye (icy moisture), perception occurs in the common sense, which is an internal faculty.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers as presented, where does perception actually occur for sight?
A) In the eye itself
B) In the common sense
C) In the object itself
D) In the Bestower of forms

Key Takeaway
According to the philosophers, perception occurs in the common sense, not in the sense organ itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You experience the world through your senses every moment. But this lesson teaches that perception is not direct—it is a constructed image that reaches a 'common sense' within you. Have you ever mistaken a vivid sensory impression for absolute reality? When was the last time a sight or sound deceived you, and how did you discover the truth? Will you now be more cautious in trusting what your senses present without questioning?
?
The philosophers say that forms flow from a 'Bestower of forms' when you face an object. That means every time you see, there is a moment of divine giving behind it. How would your daily gaze change if you acknowledged that every color and shape you see is a gift being imprinted in your soul? What would you look at differently starting today?
?
The image is in the eye, but perception is in the common sense—a hidden, inner faculty. Your external senses cannot perceive themselves; you need a deeper self that unifies them. Have you ever listened to your own thoughts or watched your own mind reflect on what you see? Are you aware of that inner witness that receives all experiences? Commit today to pause once and notice that witnessing, rather than just the seen.

Proof That True Sense Perception is Internal
Argues through size distortion and motion that real perception is inward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments from sensory distortion that prove true perception is an inner mental act, not a function of the external sense organ.

Core Idea
Sensory illusions prove perception isn't in the organ.

This passage presents a rational proof from everyday experience: if perception were literally in the eye, objects would appear exactly as they are regardless of distance or motion. Yet we see size changes and illusions, showing the real act of perceiving occurs in the inner faculty. We'll examine the geometry and the examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's reasoning come through.
2
Understand the geometric argument
The author uses the spherical nature of the eye's moisture (jalidiyya) and the geometry of sight to show that objects shrink with distance. If perception were in the eye, size wouldn't change.
Focus on how the angle narrows as distance increases.
3
Understand the illusion examples
A rotating point of fire appears as a circle, and a falling drop is seen as a line. These show the eye perceives something different from reality.
These are empirical proofs that the organ is not the true perceiver.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that real sense (al-hiss al-haqiqi) is the inner perception, not the external image. Reflect on how both arguments support this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كانت الجليدية كرية ومقابلة الكرة يكون بالمركز وفرضنا سطحا مستديرا مثلا كالترس كان يقابله على خطوط مستقيمة محيط بالترس متسع الأسفل متضايق الأعلى، ينتهي إلى الجليدية على دائرة صغيرة، وحيثما ازداد الترس بعدا ضاقت الزاوية فصغر في العين فيرى الكبير من البعد صغيرًا، فلو كان الإدراك معنى في العين وتعلق بالمدرك على ما هو به كان المرئي مرئيا على مقدار شكله وصورته، ولم يتفاوت الأمر بالقرب والبعد، وأيضًا فإن النقطة من النار إذا أديرت بسرعة أشبهت دائرة يدركها البصر، وهي في نفسها نقطة، والقطر النازل يرى خطا مستقيما وهو مستدير، فتحقق أن الحس الحقيقي ما في الباطن دون الصورة الظاهرة.
And since the icy moisture is spherical, and the facing of a sphere is by the center – and we suppose a round surface like a shield, it faces it along straight lines, the circumference of the shield wide at the bottom and narrow at the top, terminating at the icy moisture on a small circle. And whenever the shield increases in distance, the angle narrows, so it becomes smaller in the eye, thus a large thing is seen small from a distance. So if perception were a meaning in the eye and were attached to the perceived as it is, the visible would be seen according to the measure of its shape and form, and it would not vary with nearness and distance. Also, the point of fire, if rotated quickly, resembles a circle that sight perceives, while it is in itself a point; and the descending drop is seen as a straight line while it is round. Thus it is verified that the real sense (al-hiss al-haqiqi) is what is in the inner (al-batin) not the external image.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage provides two arguments to demonstrate that true sense perception is internal, not in the external organ. First, the geometry of sight: because the eye's moisture is spherical, an object at a distance appears smaller due to the narrowing angle. If perception were literally in the eye, an object would appear its true size regardless of distance. Second, perceptual illusions: a rotating point of fire appears as a circle, and a falling round drop appears as a straight line. These prove that the organ sees something different from reality, so the real perception must be a mental act in the inner sense (al-batin), not the mere external image.

Key Terms
الجليدية (icy moisture)
الزاوية (angle)
الحس الحقيقي (real sense)
الباطن (inner)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sensory illusions are errors of the sense organ.
Correction: The author uses illusions to prove that the organ itself does not perceive reality; true perception is an inner act independent of the external image.

Checkpoint
What does the example of a rotating point of fire prove according to this passage?
A) Fire can form circles
B) The eye perceives motion accurately
C) Real sense perception is inner
D) The eye has a spherical shape

Key Takeaway
Sensory distortions—size change and motion illusions—demonstrate that the true act of perception occurs in the inner faculty, not in the external sense organ.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that your eyes can deceive you about size and motion. In what areas of your life have you trusted your senses (sight, hearing, feelings) without question, only to later realize they misled you? How can you train yourself to look beyond the external image and seek the inner truth?
?
The author argues that real sense perception is internal, not in the organ. Think of a time when you perceived something negative about a person based on an external observation (their appearance or actions) but later discovered your perception was wrong. How does this lesson challenge you to not judge by the external image alone?
?
Perceptual illusions show that the eye can see something that is not real. Consider your own desires and assumptions: what 'illusions' have you been seeing in your life that keep you from recognizing the truth? What steps can you take today to align your inner perception with reality as taught by this lesson?
